des sordens	From the confusion
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Some times they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and they appear ugly and rough. And some times they cause the tooth to be black and yellow with worms until the decay reaches the gum, causing the tooth to stink; it is necessary that you hold the patient's head in your hands, and have their teeth ready under yours, until there remains nothing visible; and thus create darkness, greenness, jaundice, and other colors, as long as they are completely removed. And if what is removed at the first instance is right, it's good; otherwise, start over again on the second day and third day onward, until you have everything removed; know that teeth need various tool shapes to be extracted according to how their work shows them, because the scraper used for extracting teeth from between others has different shapes than that used for teeth outside of gaps. And these shapes and others must accompany you in your preparations.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth due to its pain that you continue to extract as long as you can, for this should not be done lightly; for it's a very fine substance up until then so one should not have any excuse for quick extraction.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull out their illness, it is necessary that you are certain about which tooth ails.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain will visit the patient, and you should be careful whether it is tooth Saint or not, and pull out the good tooth; but even so, do not leave any pain due to this, until the bad tooth has been removed. We have already wanted to do this for these doctors; and when you are certain about which tooth ails, then you must burn around the tooth right up to a depth of one millimeter to prevent gum damage from all sides; then move your hands or with your fine forceps at first try and try again until they are well loosened, then firmly hold the forceps in place. And let the head of the illness lie between your knees as Saint, and keep your hands steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the right tooth without breaking it, if it does not fall out spontaneously, take none of these instruments and insert them into each part lightly, and move it in exactly the way you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is punctured and torn, it's necessary that you fill it with cloths where the injuries are. And if you extract it gently with forceps, make sure not to break it during extraction; and it must be done very carefully under the gum line to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And always ensure you don't break it, and leave a part, and warn the patient of potentially greater pains from the root's mischief than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And remember not to act as ignorant surgeons do, who break the tooth once due to haste and bravado, without considering our advice. They instead bring forth pain from this major disease caused by the roots that remain or by breaking the tooth itself, which we have often seen; when the tooth is pulled out, wash it with wine or vinegar and salt; if bleeding occurs, as often happens, apply vinegar to it; and should that not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, to which you first speak to set teeth, should have long points and thick handles, not doubling when you pull the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick members so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be toothed to hold things in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after bleeding, it is necessary to place moistened cotton with butter on the site for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the legs are soft, and tighten the pliers called "algefi", making the patient's leg seem like a properly cared for bird; they should be done in such a way as to resemble a file, and that is their form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if they do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you expose the entire root of the object, and place the tool known as 'althali', which is called palainche, as described here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and large so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out from this, it's good; if not, use all your tools, as their shapes are shown below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if assistance is taken with this tool that has two points, which is depicted here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and there are other tools in front according to the order of the teeth, and this tool that seems like large pincers, which is illustrated here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And make sure this tool cannot be broken, and know that few tools made from bone exist; and also other tools, which are not commonly listed; and the skilled surgeons find their own instrument through themselves, according to what their work and the illness show them, for there are parts of diseases where old instructions do not teach a tool because of the variety among these and if it breaks part of the cartilage or from another bone, or if it rots, when they seek for the tools that suit him, that I have told you about, and help through gestures, as this is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be them large and well-fitting so they cannot escape but can hold and remove; then return to the arm with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it's small, take all this tool and do it:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and the shape is ugly, and especially in virgins, it must be known if the tooth was born after this tooth, and it's not straight on him, and you can neither polish nor file: then take out; and if it's alongside with this tooth, take this tool which has this form, and resembles that of two small beaks, and should be sharp in its whole length.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is inserted slowly into one's hand for the hardness of its root, and because you don't move the others, and if it appears that one could shave it off, then you shave it with a single blade in the manner depicted:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the needle file used for nails; and in filing the tooth slowly into one's hand lightly, so that you don't move it until it breaks; then smooth out at the end with a final polishing tool, and if it's too sharp it irritates the tongue, then it is necessary to file off the roughness until it becomes even, so as not to irritate the tongue or affect speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front of the socket opens, or by percussion or impact, and if the patient cannot press against what he is eating that he does not defecate, and you have cleaned them with medicine-restrictors; it is useless. If they need to be restricted by an golden thread, because silver threads turn green and decay, but gold never changes; choose threads of appropriate size neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see bleeding at the other tooth, take the thread and twist both sides between two healthy teeth, then place the ailing tooth between the diseased teeth, if there is one or more, until you see clear up to the other healthy tooth; then continue covering until reaching the part where you have been restricted, and withdraw your hand skillfully and carefully, so that it does not move at all; and bind your knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the teeth with a thread on some pliers, and unite them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not irritate the tongue; and then leave it thus constrained as much as it can last, if it comes loose, or if the threads break, if you replace them with another one; if lasts and serves thus throughout its time, and this is the arrangement of teeth and the position of the two healthy teeth and the two lower ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if you put it back in its place step by step, as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't gentle and bears it. And make no form of a bone tooth of a calf, and put it where the defect is and secure it as we have said, and remains and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time does a thread come from under the tongue or nature, that we are born thus; or by accident of healed wound; and the operations are such that you work in the mouth with the aid, and has its head on your healthy side, and lifts up the tongue; then cut this nervous line as wide as necessary until the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there's stiffness or swelling, it's due to sudden injury, if you bend the uncinate and cut the larger one; and keep in mind that the wound should not be too deep by mistake, for the artery is under it; and when you have finished, then lift up until it becomes pinkish and moistened, or cool water, then place a linen cloth on the tongue; and fumigate with the herbs each night, so that the wounds do not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood loss occurs, place the vitriol rod in his hand; and if it doesn't hurt him, apply slow-cooking fire to the cautery, which is good for this; then treat him with other remedies until he regains sanity.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it has turned to red or black or hard, and the patient doesn't feel it, do not touch it as it's gangrene; and if there's a decline towards lung disease, and there is moisture, then use the hook and drain with a subtle puncture from both sides, and then release it on both sides; and if pus won't drain in your body part, then pour vinegar over it until it stops bleeding, then return to your procedure while you're applying all the force; and once you're done, lift it using cold water or saline solution, then treat with other methods until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	removal of abscesses from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter how often it occurs within the throat cavities which are called 'godath', and they are properly known as the second pair of amonds. And when you treat them, just like we have mentioned in division, and if they do not regain sanity, be careful: If they are hard lumps with a small point and a reddish color, then don't touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron either, for fear of causing blood flow; but leave them until they heal, then you will remove them when they burst on their own or by their own force; and if they have a white coloration and the root is thin, prepare your tool for removal but first check that the abscess has drained and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit in front of the sun, and their hands should be on their stomach, and have them open their mouth and grasp the surgeon's fingers between their hands, pressing the tongue down towards all the instrument, which is this formation; and it should be made from fine silver or subtle tin as sharp as knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this tool, and see the pus? If so, take the onion and insert it into the almond shape, then pull it upwards as much as possible; remove nothing from the threads with that, then pull them away with the tool like this, seeming to be some strength. And both ways the head are curved, one place over another, and very sharp, and is made of either iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool now, then use tweezers like these.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make incisions on both sides and the other side's name; and when you have performed one of the amandres, perform the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water that is also cool or soothing, and with cold water, until bleeding occurs. Then gargle with hot water, or crusts made from cooked pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the throat is completely healed; then finish the treatment when it becomes well again. And do not let any other abscesses develop in the throat besides the two amandres, if you do them like so, equally with the two amandres.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an internal abscess that was located within her throat, which is what we call the small abscess; and had blocked off almost all of the throat well, so much that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage and thus could neither eat nor drink, and died if she continued in such condition for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had been necessary to place two ribs through each nostril from the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hurriedly performed the operation, first inserting an incision into one side, then removing it along with a large portion of flesh. Then I made another cut in the other cheek near the nose and pulled out some tissue; afterwards, I inserted the incision into the abscesses, took away a part of them, and only let out a little blood from them. And thus they were opened up, freeing the woman's throat, and she began drinking water and then wine immediately thereafter without ceasing. I continued to cut through these abscesses over a long time; the abscesses grew back almost instantly, filling the space that had been emptied only until it was quite large again. Then I stitched her up and cauterized inside her throat: so she stopped growing there. And then I left those parts, God alone knows what became of them afterwards.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the oviduct descends to the uterus, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "ovarium".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have explained in the division, and the cure doesn't help at all, and you see that the incision has healed and the pus is no longer there, but the wound is still subtle, then it's necessary to close it; and for the one that is round, compacted, not elongated; and if it is blood-stained or colored yellowish or black, then it's necessary to avoid making an incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So, when you see it, according to the manner that I have explained regarding its size and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the tool as we described earlier. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be that you do not apply force beyond the natural limit; for if you apply more than this, you hurt the voice and speech. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being burned, it must be that you use something to prevent burning when applying the cautery.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way to apply the cautery is with an intense heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient focus on your health, then press their tongue against the tool we mentioned in the chapter about cautery, and mix it with very sharp vinegar, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the force of this instrument, as shown below:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have hair where I put the medicine, like movements of a spoon, and place the instrument completely with the medicine on the eye; and make sure the disease stays stationary on its side, so that saliva and the sputum flow from their mouth to the inside of the medicine but does not go down the throat or into the ear; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour's worth, until you see that it dries and the effects of the medicine are calm; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, place the instrument entirely on the cotton in the wick, until the cotton burns on the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and then after four or five days. Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or using the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take valerian and sage and oregano and rue and chamomile and plantain and similar herbs, and gather all of them or any of them into a single pot, and place it inside, and bring it to a boil; and ensure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have one tool like hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it be silver or arsenic, and let either of the shoulder bones rest in the mouth against the side until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, while the eye is dead; after this often repeat, until the eye dries out, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the appearance of pus-filled abscesses; for many things happen here; and do not use this method when the pus-filled abscesses are declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut. Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is in the throat bone or spine of fish, where nothing happens; therefore, you should extract what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the tool, so that you can see the movement; and anything that does not open and is still in the throat, you should induce vomiting in this way until the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it gets out through vomiting; or if the badness swallows a piece of sponge, or a navel piece, or a lettuce root, or one dry bread piece; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when she comes up to you, if she is being expelled, and then pull forcefuly; and if she does not come out with what we have said, take one tool of pitch according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And make the forceps at the nose so that it can more lightly enter into the throat, and have the nose raised high above the throat. And guard yourself not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing obstructs its movement, nor push any bone inside; and when you move, let the patient feel the forceps, because if they are moved or if resistance is felt; if it goes in with a push, or if you pull hard all along the forceps equally, until it pulls hard.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the blood treated with medicine as I have explained in the division through medication treatment; and when this does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at noon, then press their tongue onto the instrument that I told you.

Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that fails, take a hair comb, and insert it into the throat of the patient, then start to comb out any blood with the comb's teeth, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you wash the patient with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full bowl of cold water and operate it in the patient's mouth, then pour it down their throat without letting them swallow, and move it around with their hand often. And as soon as the blood senses the water, they will defecate.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if they do not defecate as we have said, submerge the patient with Asafetida in the instrument used for fumigation I mentioned concerning the treatment of the eye; do this multiple times, because it will eventually pass without obstruction.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method for fumigation consists in taking a pot where there are charcoal embers, and let it be covered with a pierced cover in the middle, and on that lid place the joint of the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and have the patient hold the tip of the stick in their mouth, seal the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes until to the throat; and the saliva will now come out, if it does not do so, reapply the fumigation several times; and let the patient be thirsty and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for her to come forth forcefully through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to expel phlegm is such that when you can see it, it resembles half-moon scissors intended to enter the throat. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter concerning abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are various kinds of abscess openings and sizes, as remembered from one and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; and it's done in two ways, where one is in its own form, and the other deals with moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for those with lumps within their bodies.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For, the abscesses on the head are different from those in the base, and the abscesses of the inner thigh are different from those that come at joints. Each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if with abscesses one should not pierce them until the pulse is dead according to its accomplishment; and for those that must be pierced when they are grown, and do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses that are at joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come at joints, and it is left until it is rotten internally, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is a cause of constriction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	The abscess lies within the main limb. If you delay puncturing it until it is necrotic, it will harm the main limb. The abscess lies near the base, if you pierce or do so when it's necrotic; it should not that you puncture an abscess before full digestion has occurred, except for one lying near the base which might become fully necrotic and stay enclosed, forming a fistula; it will not heal properly in a long period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be that you know the time for perforating an abscess that has grown according to its development, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and diminution of pain and redness, and with the movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be that you place the perforation where the abscess depends more from above or below it, and at the point it opens; and make sure the perforation runs along the length of the body, whether it is on the arms or legs, in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere without any folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the fatty part of the body, it is better to let the puncturing proceed until full digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that, it will spread throughout the body with its own venom, and be full of maggots; and by chance harden its skin and its interior.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if no abscess is pierced straight through the body according to its width, as suited by the limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must introduce small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out a piece, and cover; when they have become as soft as cloth, and are drained, then you should do this just like you would with small wounds: and those that split into three angles, and those that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, similar to angular abscesses; and those where a round shape is carved out, and other shapes and cutting techniques are used.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it must be that you pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large, and has filled with much pus, if you don't drain all the pus at once in that moment, but only part of it; then leave the abscess until to another morning, then do not apply anything around it; do this repeatedly from larger to smaller, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the body is weak, or pregnant women, or young children, or elderly and decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when it tries several times with the release of the bow, that perhaps kills the patient, and you don't realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, be cautious in this chapter and when you have opened your abscess, if a wound appears, and observe whether the abscess wound is small; and if it's a plain tailor's cut, apply linen or cotton wadding. And for large abscesses, with many pus-filled cavities, you must insert one wadding into each such that they are pressed against each other. And if you have incised part of the skin in the abscess, sew it together properly, fill the cavity with old cotton or linseed rag without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then dress and apply ointment to it as long as it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your operation, quickly apply cold and ease it, wet the cloth, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is persistent bleeding, then apply control and treatment, and the powders I mentioned in this book are placed on your hands, and if it's about ice or pus, and the area is very nervous, then you should place wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on the surface; and if it's about healing, and the area is fleshed out, then apply wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days as we said, and then remove the pus and clean it up following the proper procedures until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one should act prior to the treatments of abscesses, and here comes the chapter.
des soros	of discharges
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small abscesses in the head come, and are in our ways like those on cloths, also like a button on a catkin, and many have similar appearances.

Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. And if there is a large vein root in the spot, it's not right to cut that spot at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread and let it fall out through it without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then treat.

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to treat its root, drain the pus, and stitch it up as we have said.

de squinance	Regarding lateral deviation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and talked about the surgery of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the slit of the throat, called "epiglottis," be removed; and one should not assist in this operation, because all the veins and the lung are in these who have phlegm either in their mouth or in the throat or between two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the bronchial channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis in order to prevent the loss that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut through three or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the amount of the cut at this site, not in the cartilage; and such is suitable for dividing the epiglottis so that there is no flesh and the vessels are long enough to reach.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to the entire circumference, then cut the keur until it reaches the knee; and avoid any blood vessels, should you see anything, and then cut the syphilitic, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the knee where it jumps force through the part that has been broken, and due to the loss of voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed that one doubts strangulation, assemble the two edges of the wound with care, and all the seam along the cartilage; then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis states that one should not perform this until the throat is completely swollen, and the organs are judged to be dead, and until the defect is filled.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally through their injury, and they are breathing through the wound so be protected from death. And thus it was commanded by the ancients to leave the wound open until the disease has passed, which lasts for three or four days, and then it was commanded to stitch up the wound after cleaning it when it is healed. I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife and stabbed it in her throat, cutting some channels from her heart; and I was summoned to treat her, finding her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and indeed, she did not have a severed artery or exit flow other than the throat, and the veins issued forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour. de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Lumps in the throat are called "gullet hernia," and they're large lumps of a dark purple color, occurring frequently in women; they can occur in two ways: naturally or by accident; natural ones do not have any cause.

des nous	from bones
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue. des apostemes de la marris	The treatise discusses treatments related to wounds or abscesses near the anus. The specific mention of "des apostemes de la marris" refers to managing and healing abscesses ("apostemes") located around the anus ("de la marris"). This part likely elaborates on medical practices for dealing with such conditions, possibly including procedures like lancing, medication application, dressing changes, and wound care.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in the previous section; now we will discuss hand treatments and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I state that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are due to the action of stones and the size of a sword or knife, or lance, or stick, or similar objects; or they happen according to the parts of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or head, or stomach, or belly, or liver, and similar parts; and I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head because the remembrance comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses. And if blood flow stops after treatment in that area, treat differently for the removed part; and ensure the patient is filled with wine and rich meats afterwards.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure. Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee. And the way to make the powder is: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely grind it all together. de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	From the wound of a spear or a knife.

dou derrompement dou ventre	about the rupture of the stomach
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai. You should know that belly ruptures occur through four ways: The two common stitches take place on belly wounds and stitches of other body parts have other specific stitches but are also common with other wounds; however, all of them tend to be more effective when it comes to belly wounds. When the wound is wide, and it's in the belly area, it should be that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head. Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; For small wounds, use what you have at hand. Then take the common surgical tool to cut the whole wound, stitch it up with your hands and join the edges; this is how stitches are made, and you should either use one needle or more depending on the width of the wound. Leave an inch from the edge of the wound, then insert a needle with strong thread through that part. Penetrate both sides of the skin using both needles which are inside the skin until it's pierced enough to stitch this part together; join the two ends of the stitches three times in total; then tie them tightly using thread on either side, before joining the edges of the wound. Leave an inch after each stitch, and insert another needle; then sew just as you did with the first needle, without stopping until all parts of the wound are stitched; use needles that are neither too fine nor too thick, because thin needles cut through the flesh completely, while very thick ones may not fit well: these must be medium-sized. Don't let the stitches pierce or loosen during sleep by being too tight at the edges; cover them with blankets or cloths to help hold together until healed; this method of stitching is more suitable for small wounds, as you would use one needle and a second stitch in most cases when you join both sides of the skin and both sides of the siphac together on one needle with medium thread; once you've pierced all four ends together, pull the needle from where you started, doing it like you tie knots. Leave space between each stitch equal to about an inch; this stitch heals the person, and I sewed a wound that was caused by a knife in their stomach region, which had been cut open with a sword, being more than half a palm wide, and contained intestines several inches long, being in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines until it had been 24 hours since they were removed, and the wound healed up to 15 days. I treated him and he became healthy again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when the doctors had decided that he would die, it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a region where none could be found, nor any medicines; instead, I changed old cotton twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you two proper sewing methods: take the needle and insert it from the outside of the wound to inside; when it pierces straight through the muscle in line, sew with your hand at the point where the needle pierced or near what you have pierced, then make another piercing on the opposite side of the inner part to the outer edge; and know that this sewing technique is like how a peltier sews fur, leaving once the insertion site from one side and taking it up again from the other, until all parts are completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, as Galen properly stated, is such that no one does it. They join the two parts together in their natural order and apply one end near another, like this: thread a needle or an eye near the middle, then pierce only the top part, leaving both ends joined at the middle; then turn the needle and make it pierce from below all the way to inside, through both ends joined at the middle. Then pierce both parts from below all the way to inside with two more needles or eyes that are on the opposite side; this is the manner of stitching and is the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word and no one affirms it, that one must stitch the belly with two needles or threads in each; and should one pierce one needle on one side and the other on the other, like those who stitch corroies. And know that when the injury is halfway through the belly, the stitching is more painful than the others' bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments on the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is this way; when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just like the flesh has had them, then return the intestines, and the belly; then put on a stimulating powder over the char. And if the flesh has had them, place no ointment until the wound heals; and clean the thread, have it sutured together the opening, and the mirror; then treat the wound as others are treated, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to heal properly, old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine besides several preparations when the wounds are simple; and if you suspect that the wound might cause communication with principal members, then it is necessary for you to moisten light wool in oil of gently heated warmth or in rose oil, and place it inside the joints, and around the armpits; and if there is pain or inflammation in the bowels, and this happens repeatedly, then catheterize with black wine, and similarly if the inflammation reaches up to the intestines; and puncture from within, and know that when it's large intestine, it's easier to heal than smaller ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called 'juvenile' cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the position of the veins found there, and because of the intricacy of the entire body's structure, as well as its connection with nerves.

de la routure dou boueil	Of the breach of the boil

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or where it might be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called 'fistula', and even when covered and healed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division. dou feu	The fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.
