Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the symptoms of this vein's beginning occur, so that there is a very large inflammation in the leg, then it changes the veins, and the vein begins to exit outside, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder joint has been opened, it must be enveloped internally with a piece of leather that is three-quarters to one-and-a-half inches and then sewn up. Leave the leather on the leg, and every time there's any left over before sewing, envelope it again inside the leather and sew it up; if it's too long, cut off some part of it and re-envelop until everything has come out; because if you cut it, it enters the flesh and causes pus formation or infection in the area leading to a bad disease; so this thing must be treated gradually until the whole length is done, leaving nothing behind at all. And when this vein has been treated for five palms of length, or ten, approximately half a day later than when it started treating from that palm length, and when you cut it off, keep one raisin or piece of grain, then pierce until to the bottom, so that everything can come out; and evacuate all matter inside and administer medicine against putrefaction every day after that, then treat as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein use cold hands, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or heel, where there's much loss and where the pain jumps; then therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that spring up between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle illness", because it has affected many cattle, and it's a little worm that springs up between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body rising and falling. The pain can be felt from member to member until it breaks through the skin where it was heading, and jumps out; and is accompanied by putrefaction of some bodily fluids, such as coming worms and snakes and maggots and roundworms in the stomach; and one wonders about its malevolence, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eyes, sometimes it returns and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, one cannot help but observe that when it's going: therefore, it's necessary that you bind the head above and below with a very tight strong bandage, then cut upwards and treat it immediately, and ensure it goes straight into the flesh; if you don't find any, then use fire cautery on it until it heals; and the greater damages it causes are when they go towards the eyes, as we have said; and should you see it approach or head close to the eye, then tightly bind under him the eyebrow in a form, cut upwards, and treat immediately; it's advisable to use the hand of purification of the body from medicines that dissolve for the illnesses produced by humors, and beware of cooked meat causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it brings about pain that comes to any limbs, and then spreads from limb to limb; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a patient with an illness, and they showed me their arms, revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm; shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything else, like quick silver when cut from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled into the shoulder, then later spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then they told me it was winding around inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how she moved thus member by member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In any case, I wanted many times to move the pain from one place to another as well, but I didn't actually do it like what I saw in the woman; and I thought that was because she had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and due to this there appeared this constriction of wind; and they don't seem to notice according to this reason among those who are delicious and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see treat this illness, and the patients feel that pain, if it opens as we have said, quickly over and under, then press on so that the wind pressure released from the body comes out; and cauterize the body; and if you do not see it at your eyes, treat the one who removes the wind pressure, such as fetid pills, pill of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	Des saiettes" translates to "of arrows" in English. This term refers to objects that resemble arrows, likely used in the context of medical practices or treatments involving piercing or insertion into the body. In medieval contexts, such terminology could relate to various implements or procedures associated with traditional medicine or surgery.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary, according to their appearances and according to the locations on the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small ones, and those that are barbed, and soldered; and there are some with two angles, and others with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that excretes in any member does so according to two ways: or in a primary body it pierces, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar bodies.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she coughs then in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you be prepared for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterward in various situations; and when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not been fully removed, if you can, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow punctures and enters the bone, and a fluid emerges from beneath the head at the site of entry, is along with blindness, numbness, vertigo, redness in eyes, inflammation and reddening of the tongue, spasms and confusion of mind, vomiting of bile; sometimes without strength coming through the nose or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; and a moist white blistering sign at the wound that resembles pus, and also burns like charred flesh; and if this sign appears, take it seriously and remove the arrow if possible.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it exits or pierces the heart is that it is close to the left breast, and feels also as though it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and by chance if the arrow stops moving like a pulse, and black blood comes out, and brings on coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never goes into the flesh is when there's no foam spurting from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient has a changed color, and they sigh loudly with a hot forehead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow has exited through the buttock's cover, it is beneath the small ribs; and produces great pain and sighing; and moves all limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if it's an arrow or stomach, by chance if there is no matter from the meat undigested in the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if it's an arrow or stomach, and in the case of a jump there is no dung passing through the intestines, then there is no hope in treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if it's an arrow or stomach in the bladder, and urine comes out by jumping and leaves, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and chest and neck and shoulder blades and the shoulder joint and the spine of the back and the ribs and the kidneys and the legs, and similar body parts, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in one's nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do that other thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one man that an arrow hit him in the left lung at the root of his nose: I tested it and pulled it out from another side under the ear's fat, without causing much pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he pulled out an arrow that had hit him in the ear fat under the paper, and the arrow was stuck, but could not be reached beyond the head of the shaft. The wound was large like a Turkish bow, completely without ears; the player was healed and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And remove an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and that arrow was the Arabian ear one: I would cut off the stubble, then carefully extracted it until I pulled out the arrow, making the Christian healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And remove an arrow from the house, that it was stuck in his chest or belly, and I thought he would die; and then after passing thirty days, if it didn't change its position; I cut into the arrow, extracted it, and pulled it out, with no ill event.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a house to which an arrow fell or was struck on its back, and the wound is sealed up; and the arrow stays inside, and does not change its natural position, nor does it find harm in any of its natural actions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And look at another man, who got hit by an arrow in his face, and had stitches put into the wound; and ever since has suffered great pain; and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was an arrow in the king's garden for the princes, which stuck out through his nose, slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was already in place when I was summoned to treat it three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound severely constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a subtle treatment to it, and did not feel anything penetrate; yet he felt pain and discomfort in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it might be due to the tip of the arrow. I placed a moist adhesive dressing over his ear for this reason, as his ears did not swell up; and I saw the appearance of the arrow in his ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster on the first day and treated the wound immediately. The patient endured long periods of pain, until the arrow was felt inside his nose on the second day; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive arquebuse medicine on the wound each day until it opened, and I tested it; felt the tip of the arrow which was moving towards its location. Then adjusted within the opening using that corrosive arquebuse medicine until the head of the arrow became visibly apparent; passed through well for approximately four months, then healed the wound so thoroughly that I applied forceps on one side and the other, but could not remove it; hence began to refine and invent ways with instruments until I found how to use well-made forceps in accordance with its shape as described towards the end of this chapter; used these forceps while treating and healing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the judges rule that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it thus, and after the wound was sutured, he was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting arrows, so that you should apply your treatment to what I do not say, because books can't cover everything; but wise masters compare well on a small number of things, and on what is current and lacking, they find new work and new tools, dealing with the removal of foreign substances that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I state that arrows enter the body or limbs through two ways: either from their entrance point or from another side; and if they enter through a muscle, it's an internal arrow penetrating flesh, and now it doesn't occur at all.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it be until the bone is rotten inside and has healed outside; and similarly if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, let it stay like that for a few days, removing some each day; and then it will jump. If it still doesn't jump, puncture through to every small hole internally, as long as the veins are wide inside, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone near the head, and reaches up to one of the lungs inside the brain, or if any of the situations I've described happen to the patient: don't remove it immediately, but let it be until it becomes equal after a few days; because if the arrow comes up to this depth, it's a death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not penetrate until its shaft, and remains with no injury to the patient for several days without any bad incident, then the device of removing it should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly placed in such a way and cannot come out at all,
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body but not seen, if it touches all parts of you; and if you feel it, if you try to remove it with no suitable tool; and if due to the wound's constriction or the depth of the arrow, there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then make the wound larger; and try to remove the arrow when possible, and if it has ears that hold it in place, cut out any flesh that is stuck from two sides until you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can while trying to remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you will more easily pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't remove it in one go, let the shaft be buried up to its feathers until it's broken, then pull it out, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood goes against this, then carry out what we have said about treatment in our chapter; and be cautious about incisions near nerves and veins, and use your skill to extract the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them, as this is their greatest help, and if you can't do that, then lay them down according to how the sign shows them.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that came from the other side, or where something protrudes through him, or if the skin is swollen in a way that we see or feel differently: cut there, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then squeeze: if it leaps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your hand around it as long as it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it there for now, and then continue the extraction until it does; and if part of the arrow is inside him, force it all the way in; and if it's just lodged, and you see how to apply pressure, if I provide the instrument, so that the point of the arrow goes into the notch of the tool; and then press hard, and if the arrow is stuck, if I apply the instrument with a point entering inside, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow touches the body, you should cut all the flesh around where it enters, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow penetrates or passes through the chest or bladder or abdomen, and it is close to organs, you should cut upwards, if possible. And take care not to cut into the blood vessel or nerve, then remove it, and then stitch up the wound, when needed; and treat until healing occurs.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used for arrows resembles an bird's beak, and here is the form:

des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common bodies
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which we bleed are thirty-one, of which there is or its head sixteen, that being: two that come after the ears, which are called "two herbs"; and the two arteries in the two temples visible; and two vessels that are in the two eyelids, those are called "suckers"; and the vein that is inside the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose; and the two glands in the neck; and the two veins above the mouth's lips, and these are the veins called "augerich"; and two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that we usually heal are found in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it's on the left side, which people commonly call the "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'fascial', composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; people commonly refer to this as the "vein of the heart". The basilic vein is found either on the left or right side of the body, which people call the "vein of the belly", and it's located under the clavicle, and it's precisely the one that we heal, opening clearly over the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The salvatelle is the vein located between the little finger and ring finger, and it can be found twice (II rains). La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like cords to the surgeon, and there are such that are full of windiness, so when you place them over the flame, they pull away from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus belong to these. Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good; if not, try again slightly under or at once near that spot, where the limb is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite. Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should drink honey syrup and half of an aromatic wine that's between old and new, and they should fast for a little while, then eat small pieces of pork, and young birds, and baby pigeons; on the day when they are being suctioned, they should drink more than they eat. It is good to give some people triamcinolone or muscatel before suction therapy, or after, to strengthen their main limbs; and cool down his head, but it is not recommended that those who are hot drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed to cause irritation are those that are placed on the liver, and on the lungs, and in the case of podagre (gout), and on the abdomen and belly button and kidneys, and hip. For this member doesn't suffer from being pierced by needles, and we do it only to draw blood from one part of the body to another, just as when we place them on nipples when a baby is breastfeeding; for removing the viscosity in the body, we place suction cups on the abdomen and belly button to decrease its size. And removes pain when there's swelling or stone, and by its attractive power it may remove the swelling accidentally, or empties the stone from its place; thus it does when you put it on the liver and lungs where there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty solely for the purpose of sucking. They are not given together with heat applied, and they are filled sometimes with boiling water, as in diseases such as pleurisy, and in this manner we fill the suction cup with hot water or water in which it has cooked useful herbs to that end.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used over fire is like this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And take two fingers of half a palm each way, and place it at the cost of one thousand in the middle, just as to push a needle out, whether iron or silver, before doing so ensure that it doesn't hurt the sick person upon placing it on the limb; have a rod halfway across either from an iron frog or iron, for placing a candle holder, and they should be great and small according to diseases and the condition of those who use them; because suction cups for children are different than those for adults, and lighter ones for skinny people compared to fatty ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And we should thus place this suction cup onto the limb: take the candle holder or a line of wax and place it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, ensuring that the light reaches the bottom of the suction cup to prevent burning the sick person; and then put it on the limb, and hold your fingers over the part we mentioned, so when you wish, if steam comes out, remove the suction cup; and take the wax line as before and repeat this often, should you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup then, administered in the illness of pleurisy, there is no need for a needle or a lancet at all stages, and it should only be used when full of water, and placed on the limb solely; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without needles are administered only to limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in their clean state of flesh, like thigh or calf bones, and other similar parts; and the quality of use is that when you find withouts in sweet waters free from debris, take them; and place one in sweet water until they are familiarized, and have nothing inside the womb; and then lance and suction them, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place them on the withouts; and once they become full, and start to leak, if there is a limb where one can put a suction cup, put it, for this lasts not long after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the shoulder in warm water and cool water very well, then rinse it. And when the skin is well on the body of the wounds, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and place it there until the wounds are dry; and if the wounds are many, put powdered vitriol or garlic, or similar things, until they are dry; or you put half of peeled beans under the shoulder and leave them until they roast on the shoulder, which will stop the bleeding now; and if you need more, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not close properly, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or you insert a needle there until some pus comes out, and then put it back in. As soon as they start smelling of blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are expelling pus, you can sprinkle a little myrrh and finely ground wheat flour, or ashes, which should heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are useful for restoring breaks and alleviating suffering.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the people who are reading this chapter were never shown or read anything like it in old books; for this reason, this knowledge has been hidden in our land because I have never found anyone skilled at it. And I know nothing of this skill other than through the studies and experiences from ancient texts and through my own practice and understanding over a long life, also based on experiments. Herein, I've outlined what's contained within this chapter clearly and summarized it for simplicity in conclusion, also making sure to explain each tool being used so as to be easily understood; similar to how I have done in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we introduce or give an outline of the content of this book and the chapters in which wisdom places its understanding, staying on the truth, so that those who have experienced it can know and learn this noble craft, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I state that when there is fracture or dislocation or twisting or strangulation in any part, it's necessary to attend swiftly to the patient from one side and another, without letting anything hinder you, such as weakness of limbs, children, old people; or if their touch is too hot, or too cold; and refrain from consuming cool meats, this means chilled cuts, liver and venison, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats. And don't fill them with too much meat that fills the veins with blood until you're sure of no pus to come out in an abscess, or spreading of matter inside their limbs; if they recover under their first regime of treatment which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary for the patient to consume meats that cause excessive swelling or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and peas, and pies, and beef, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And with such swelling the break begins to heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in old or decrepit people cannot be healed or sutured according to their nature due to the drying of limbs, or those which are too soft, such as a child's bones; but apply first aid, set the bone broken and press tightly against it until it is reunited with the limb, as it was before; do not rush in completing your work, for this requires large meat to nourish him afterwards, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	Know that breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break in the head is different from a break in the heel, or of the leg, and I will tell you all ways of breaks in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that occur at the elbow, and others when striking, as when sharpening a feather to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there's breaking with injury, and breaking at all a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each way it has its tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings back to his mind; and he recognizes the breaking of the bone by the twist in the limb and the good opening through which well comes out, and the pressure from the hand; and when there is no twisting or injury to the joint, and the patient doesn't feel much pain, if there's no breaking; but it can have a twisting, or a small crack.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gradually tighten it now in a subtle manner.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breach which went in the arm, and are the two parts separated, now they must put them on equal terms, so that abscesses dress at both ends; and if abscesses become hard again, you let him not stay one day, until the abscesses are relieved; then put it evenly with the muscles that you can gently and wisely apply, and know that his restoration is easier than those of whom he has pieces; then tighten as described later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, and it is divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or near your hand with a small member, or at two strings, or at one string and by your hand; place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the injured parts of the member are healed, you gently adjust all additions in their places as much as you can, and take care not to cause any injury or pain through your work. And properly align both ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it doesn't seem to be in the right place: if you dress it beautifully, and don't pull too much, not squeezing as those who extract by their own surgical method do, pulling at the abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often wished.
