And when the limbs are healed, ensure that you do not move the patient, neither while awake nor asleep, nor on changing position or in any other manner; and make sure that the limb is securely set so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when the patient no longer feels any pain, it is not yet fully healed. It must be placed in a suitable position so that they do not feel any pain; and you should ensure that it is put straightly, making sure there is no twist once restored; and this quality of the injured limb depends on what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied in smallness and largeness, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And for smaller limbs, such as arms and legs and alike: it is necessary to envelop them in soft and delicate linen cloths; and for those that are large, like stomachs and thighs: it is necessary to wrap around with a broad and firm bandage, because the broad bands embrace the entire large limb evenly from all sides, making sure there's no twist. Then tie up light bandages around three or four times depending on the size of the member and keep your hand firmly on each band until you reach the broken area, then move to above the break and apply less pressure, so that the break can move slightly away; and gradually soften the bandage little by little, until most of the healthy part is covered, then start again with another layer of bandages around the broken limb. After this process, return to the area below the break and apply moderate pressure without being too tight or too loose, as we have explained in the previous chapter; then place linen or cloth strips between the bandages until they are evenly spread out, and finally secure everything with a belt and properly made pins if there's no pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing to the area, which reduces the swelling and leaves it thus for a few days; then press upon your points, and they should be of half the width of a thick rod evenly sharpened, or from wood used to make joints, or palm fronds, and align them according to this pattern:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the points you place on the break be slightly larger and wider than the others; and should be as long as appropriate for the size of the limb or its magnitude; then press upon the points in the same way you did with the first application, then tie them above with a supplemental string as was done with the first application on the breakage; more tightly at first, then less so; and it is necessary that the string be medium in size, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; because if the string is large like those who make their string for sewing linen cords, which is a great mistake, as the application cannot be even if it is too fine, and it does not suit having less than half a finger's width between each point.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the pins after compression in their healthy areas, then you should apply linen or matted wool to them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is irritated and the ribs are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to constrain all broken limbs on their first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not suitable to use these hot plasters for more than five or seven days, or according to the severity of the abscess, depending on its occurrence; and here is the way of using ancient plaster methods to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: you take flour that stands near mill walls and mix it with plenty of egg, creating a mixture not too thin nor too thick. Use this concoction as needed, and this is the common method of restoring fractures in various ways, even for women and young children, as neither too hot nor too cold should be used.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a restorative plaster for fractures and dislocations: take three parts each of garlic, dandelion leaves, rue, asafetida, and Arabic gum, totaling nine parts; add five parts each of myrrh and aloes; use seven parts of vinegar. Make this into a powder, mix it with plenty of eggs; if the mixture is warm, apply this plaster, for it has good composition, it quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plastering method suitable for torsion: take mastic and myrrh oil, each in quantity of XIII parts; myrrh and aloes in quantity of IX parts; castor oil VI parts; Armenian balm in quantity of X parts. Grind them well together, mix with vinegar or plenty of egg, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of splinting joints and fractured bones at their sites, and alleviating the pain arising therefrom, and when cutting bone and making incisions: take new wool, and grease it in oil and cooking fat, and place this on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Bandages do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly relieving pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that sets broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poplar leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of splinting for the repair of bone fracture and to ease the removal of pus.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of sweet basil, chamomile, violet flowers, tansy flour, one part from each; and grind them, then mix with wine. If the affected limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to reattach more firmly than the first, when an abscess-hard comes to repair on the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and sesame seed, balsa wood, melilot, and sansucius, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all take one part; grind and mix with the water of salt, or sweetened water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that when restoring strength to a broken limb, one should only apply cerate made from wax and oil, and not any other substance. He states it should be applied between two layers so as not to be too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems like Galen suggests we should apply something on the broken limb for restoration, with somewhat dry but slightly warm substances, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering suitable for injury and pain: take the fat and feathers from cooked chickens, or bird feathers, and vinegar, and equal parts salt, and grind them together to make a plaster mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little later, and be careful so that the patient does not feel any pain or is hurt by his own bone in its place; if you do not remove it with your hands and when pain comes to the member, or itching, without rest or swelling, if this happens, act quickly and remove it, and reapply the dressing now. Take a light cloth and a wet sponge, dip them into water, then soak up your limb until the itching stops, and the pain is eased; then let the member rest for an hour, then place it on dry bedding, moistened in water or rose oil, and secure it with a bandage, until you are sure that the abscess has cooled. And calm down the inflammation of the limb, and remove any pain, then start applying a subtle reattachment, and a little more dressing, but do not apply pressure as before; and continue to handle carefully until they heal properly.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus has formed and turned red, along with pain and swelling, indicating bone inflammation throughout, then you will need plaster and bandaging, so restart the process as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there's no effect on the limb that we have mentioned, or it wasn't freed until after three days, four, five, seven; and each time leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the swelling subsides, and approaches the alignment of the flesh; then tighten more than at first, and let its body grow, as I said previously; and if you notice that the limb has dried excessively beyond what is necessary, know that there will be no new ones here; take it out in hot water every time you free it, and each third day, clean a bit of the wound; through this process cut off any remaining tumors on the limb, and quickly correct what foolish healers do who bend the limb improperly: it's bad practice, and this is shameful work, and I don't see anything else than to let it dry properly and open it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and they come in various forms. Each has its specific causes; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, where the collarbone breaks up to just below the shoulder joint, as happens with an axe or staff hit; due to this kind it is called this fracture method "ax-breaking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and these are the large or small injuries from these two kinds of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or fracture in the bone, or through stone, or on stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break halfway through, reaching up to the membrane that surrounds the bone or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is healed within the bone just as thin as a hair, and the crack small, this kind of breakage is called "hairline" fracture due to this reason; and if the injury occurs by hitting with stone or falling down, or through similar actions causing part of the bone piece to enter from below, resulting in its edges cutting so deeply like the candlestick when it's heated on the candle holders; then the rock inside penetrates.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often in those with soft bones like an infant's head; and it occurs through all these types of fracture resulting in small bone fragments being dislodged, such as pips; and I will discuss this in its appropriate section.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all the ways of breaking through extraction from them, and the examination with rods, and through the putrid matter which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair's appearance is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it inwards, if the breaking is blackened, then it indicates the break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be careful about any adverse event involving the organs and if you do not see any harmful incident such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever ague, and if the eyes start to come out and turn red, or other similar signs in various conditions, then cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming event, yet still hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes before you, and it's time for surgery, then you should remove the bone fourteen days after the operation.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's summer, hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes gangrenous, and let us encounter the events that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if breaking of the bone reaches up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to split the broken part in this manner: and take hold of the skull at its soft spot, and uncover all along the bone in every way possible, and along the shape of the wound as much as possible, and when bleeding comes with uncovering the bone, or if there's pus present, assist yourself with what is necessary, and ensure that you fill the space with wet cloths in olive oil; then let the wound rest until the pus has subsided and the bleeding stopped; only afterwards may you begin to remove along the bone, this is done according to two ways of operation: one way is that you trim at a tight cut upfront, and that's the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then do another larger cut than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, they should be pointed and made of iron; and apply them lightly, making sure not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is far and hard, you should pierce it internally, in such a way that you administer cuts with needles, not completely piercing through the bone but ensuring there's a margin of about half a circle above the tip, so as not to let the tip pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each goes into its place under the thickness of the bone, in such a way that you have needles for all parts; and this is the form of the three ways of using needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing internally through the bone is to place one needle on the bone and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced. Then put the needle elsewhere a little later, and do this all internally, then scrape out the space between the fragments of the bone using the incisors, doing so more finely and gently than possible, as we have said, just until you bring the bone to your hand or none of the instruments that you are using such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is fitting to prepare an incision tool that remains from the bone to all other tools similar to a tooth cutter. But it must be more secure and more delicate than another tooth cutter; if there's nothing left of the small bones or no scales, then lightly scrape with some instruments; afterwards treat the wound with dressings and applications as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of operation is this, which Galen stated, it being more secure; and he had the strength of a lion, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to expose a portion of the bone, at the place where the fracture opens and moves, so that once you have exposed that part, you will place under the edge of this lens-shaped incision, as described below:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is divided into two sides, so that when cutting it faces the bone; then strike with a small hammer on this side, so that you gently hit the entire bone, and take good care of the cloth that is nearby; if it sticks to the bone, lightly pull it, because you will pull out the bone well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut from above, with small pieces remaining, it's necessary to address that roughness afterward. You should remove the scales using a finely sharp razor tool, which you must have in various quantities, to apply according to each location, considering both the method and the appearance of the breakage.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	When dealing with large razors, and then progressing to finer ones, you should continue this process until it is done properly.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each other kind of fine hair trimming and delicate breakage, you should proceed according to its direction; this is something that cannot be adequately handled by someone who has devoted their studies to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the boil is uncovered, then it should be covered with a linen cloth according to the size of the wound. Then moisten it in olive oil and place it over the wound; take another double layer cloth made from two or three layers, moisten it in wine and olive oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this gently as you can, without burdening the boil, then apply another bandage above that, using force only enough to touch the wound itself. Leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess becomes calm, then remove the bandage and administer medicines such as rosemary roots, flour of vinegar, incense powder, arnica, and similar substances; from these make a powder, apply it over the wound, and administer further medicinal treatments that do not cause discomfort. And watch that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor let anything assemble into clumps because when such things assemble on the cloth covering the brain, they corrode and rot, causing great harm to the patient; for if something is placed on the boil that is irritant, it will burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be careful, should no mishaps come to the patient as we have said, if there is doubt then you must consider it doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no danger arises only because of the medicine we have applied, and this virtue has been effective, then you should take one part of honey, three parts of almond oil and a drachm of glue, and place it on your face; then treat it in accordance with appropriate treatments until it heals, as long as it is clean.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts near the nose, or even one alone, is broken, for these are two bones. And the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, nor will it allow force to bend or twist it, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should pinch your little finger or nostril and apply equal pressure to that break inside your index finger, and through your nose outwardly until the nostril revives according to its natural form; and do this gently, and be careful not to allow any pain to affect the patient with your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and can't reach the nostril, it's necessary that you place it level with the tip of a finger slightly thicker.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, redo the process, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has healed, then pinch at the nose's tip with lint bandages, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another poultice on the other side, if there is a break; and make them large enough to fill the depressions around the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorative suggests mixing with butter, and changing each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I believe it might not be correct, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture from an egg and powder of mill; then let the tent stay until the bone is hard, and the cartilage tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And once put on or use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have one egg's worth of down covering them, and if the dressing stays intact, let the wound be exposed, letting air flow through; now do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses come to the nose as you treat them, then apply a poultice or wet cotton in oil, or a small portion of garlic juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess has not burst outwards, then apply a plaster on top, made from sandalwood powder and incense powder, mixed with an egg yolk. Then place it under light bandages, without tying them too tight; and should any breakage occur due to pressure beneath the nose being small, and if broken into tiny pieces, then use instruments suitable for this purpose, then cut along the wound line, applying healing things in a sequential manner, and joining tissues back together. If there is no injury within the nose itself, and nothing needs curing on the tent, then insert cloves until it's healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured externally, and there's no wound outwardly visible, only the breakage occurs externally. It isn't broken into two halves solely by cracks internally; one can easily recognize this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you press your index finger into the mouth at the patient's chin; and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then press your index finger of your right hand, gently pressing the fracture internally, and push it outward with the other hand, ensuring both are equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is an fracture of the jawbone in two parts, it then requires that you perform an extension of both parts, ensuring they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And when the movements of teeth occur, or breakage, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place on the broken mandible some wadding, and put over it one double layer; then place upon the layer a large wedge well made, or a piece of leather equal in size to the length and width of the mandible. Secure this to the muscles that you can, and command the patient to rest, eating light meat portions.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if it loses its shape by the third day, and then return to fixing what has become loose; apply plaster over it, made with powder from the mill mixed with enough egg or flour of wheat, after removing the wadding; place over the plaster a light cloth, and if the plaster sticks and the patient's position doesn't change, leave them as they are until they heal. Many times they heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if there are incisions that become infected, then apply what we have told you many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is breaking together with injury, reward none of the bone pieces that are removed; if such delicacy requires tools suitable for this task.

de la brisure de l’espaule	On the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	regarding the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that are between the handle and the shoulder of the arm; if it is broken, one must restore it according to either of two ways: out of which one way involves taking a single solid rod with medium thickness, in such form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And fasten these two heads together with two threads, and weave them upwards, then place the wound on one spot; then pour the broken arm onto the rod until it reaches halfway, having formed half of a rod's bend, then position above anything or where helpers are below; then place the eyes of the fracture equally among their hands, so long as the broken part returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie. And if the irritation is close to the top of the shoulder, you should put one end of the bandage halfway between sitting up and on top of the irritation, and the other towards the knife, under the irritation; and also if the irritation is in front of the knife, you should place one end lightly, without effort, until the irritation is even under the left side and on the right side; then apply the irritation evenly as necessary, and extract, so that no pus comes out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come about under the wound, do not strain it until after seven days, and place on it moistened linen in oil and rose water, until the abscesses under the wound are soothed; then strain it, and how to strain it should be that you put plaster over the wound, then join the arm to the shoulder support, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; place the bandage and hold it tight over the shoulder support, and over the arm, so that the arm is in its usual position, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use weights and place an extra large and strong weight over the tear, and leave one space of about two inches between each weight, and let each weight be big enough to pass through the wound three inches from both sides; then strain on those weights as I said at the beginning of this chapter on tearing wounds, more strongly but less when pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the base of the bone and its constriction, as we have said, in the place where you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt about the abscess at that spot, if you let it be bound for a whole week, as we have said; then check every three days the bond, to ensure no itch spreads over it or any pus cannot come into the limb because it might be too tightly bound.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come about, or if the dislocation takes more than three days and then heals on its back with hands on its stomach; place one cloth full of equal wool under the shoulder. And each hour during day or night, check whether the figure of the broken limb is still intact or if the bindings have softened; if the address responds through medicine's virtue, and it gives meat as we have placed before you, in such a way that the meat becomes fine and tender at first; and when it starts to heal back, if it becomes large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be repositioned within forty days from the start; then one must loosen them, give baths, and administer ointment medications for the pain to subside.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tangled, it should be kept for untangling for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Regarding the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are named the 'foscile' pair. One bone is small, it forms the pocket; and another one is large, it rests under the small finger; by chance if only the large foscile breaks or the small one, or they both might unite together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing. And when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's only the small bone that is broken, then it should be stretched slightly and made equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, then it should be strained harder; and extend to the first joint, and hold the hand pouch higher than the others, and place the smaller fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the bones cross themselves against themselves, and the first joint in front higher than the bones so they do not suffer any strain; then extend your attendants' arms up to her wrist or elbow, and another attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes even, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking into pieces, you place each one of them back in its place, and if there is no bone pierced that touches the skin, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut through the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in dealing with wound injuries, I've spoken about them individually; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the beginning of the reattachment abscesses form, then apply a poultice made from oil and white beeswax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the poultice in such a way that when the abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And apply the wax, then put on the plaster made from powder mixed with plenty of egg whites. Place the needles, and if necessary, increase the force by one more than usual; make sure it's a bit wider than the other ones. Know that there should be six or seven needles arranged in various positions: either inside an osseous structure, two needles can do this; hold them closer to the sore area than elsewhere, as you did at the start of this chapter; and keep the plasters covering the sore moist and soft, they should not harden or become abrasive. The threads used for sewing are made from linen, neither too thick nor too thin; these details were explained earlier.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And heal the member and the bond after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad incidents happen to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary for you to immerse the member in hot water until the itch subsides; and let the member not be left to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the process of traction. If the ligaments are torn and the bones are exposed, do as seems appropriate.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no injuries can occur to the limb due to it being too tight, it is necessary that you soften (the material) a bit. leave like this for several days until the injuries heal, and then start compressing again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said happens to the patient, or if the release does not occur up until the 20th day.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or elsewhere, then place their hands on his neck, and if his necks are equal, and take care of movement and restlessness, and sleep on his back; and know that this cure is restored in thirty days or forty-five, and sometimes in twenty, according to the compositions and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	from the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and in us, there are few breaks, and it only results in many foldings.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or folded, it is necessary for the patient to lie with their head crossed and facing straight ahead equally; then they should place their hand on an extended table, and extend the broken fingers, placing them in a straight line as much as possible. They must be well aligned, then apply plaster and wafers if there's no pus. After that, place one stick according to the size of the hand; and wrap it with a piece of linen, making sure to cover it with one yard of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the breakage is in the part around the belly of the hand's heel, make a sphere from cloths, and instruct the patient to stretch it towards their broken heel. Then stretch it with a long cloth, and place the stick straight down as much as needed so that its height matches the heel of the hand, and stretch it accordingly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the breakage occurs at the front, it is necessary that you place a splint above, and another under on the sole of foot, so that the hand remains open and upright, then tie them completely around the hand, and seal the connection between fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breakage happens at one of both feet, which is a sprain, in such a way as it should; and you press with the sole, and if you see that placing a small upright splint helps to lift the breakage and keeps it from moving. And if the breakage occurs on other toes, like in the index or among others, do it similarly by pressing evenly and then tie them using a healthy toe afterward; or tie all of them together when walking as well, holding firmly, or place a splint over it, like one would with a sprain. Take care in preserving the position and location of each dressing individually, and prepare for those who come after you, just as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the elbow is often broken, and one can see this when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration comes in two ways. One involves tying above the break, and another involves tying below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their face, then extend each minister's joint equally to their equal part; and this is when the break has entered into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thumb, then let one ligament be towards the knife, and the other ligaments under the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it's near the knee, then let the ligaments be inside the knee, and let it be a flexion downwards; then place the points of the bone to its two hands until it is according to its natural figure, and then apply plaster, and bind it, should pus not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess to remove, let it heal then return to your work and treatment; the wound has been treated in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary for you to wrap around the break with a two or three times doubled strip of hard bandage, and leave the excess. Then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the ankle, and insert a long thread along the thigh under the knee. Let the head catch the thread above it; then turn the leg and thigh bands over and over again. Then place plaster around the break, put an asterisk on the bone of the leg; then insert eight strips between the leg and thigh with a wet cloth to make sure there is equal tension. Begin by wrapping three or four times around the break; and as you go above the break, loosen it less. Then pull two threads that you have inserted between the leg and thigh for three asterisks above it, turn back down to under the head of the thread until you reach below the foot; and tighten it, so that it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this, and should there be no pus or swelling or other symptoms.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if this happens, should it loosen, and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch, then they must be extracted when possible; and if one cannot do so, it is necessary to cut the skin open and drain the pus; and treat it as we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the flesh broken when these rods are applied in places like on the shoulder and arm; yet still, upon completion of such treatment, there is no damage to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the flesh is restored within one month or perhaps slightly more or less, depending on the variety of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the kidney
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint area there is little cracking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, except for just a crack, or if the joint is dislocated, it affects every wound and senses of pain, and this can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.
