de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg are two bones, of which one is called straight or "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and there occurs every injury or breakage as it does in the arm. And its restoration is similar to that of the arm alike, and the techniques are all the same. And if both these bones get broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bones are broken, turn towards the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; then it twists around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	So proceed with stretching, and make it even, then evenly tie the joints; but still, if there is roughness in the breakage, and there are several fragments, that the stretching should be less and more gentle; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two ropes of fust that support the leg on both sides, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee to below. Then wrap these in two layers of cloth, one above and one below, bind them in the middle, and at this binding ensure that the leg cannot decline towards the right or left; it should be well done this way; and no one administers a belt as long as the leg, made of fust, and puts on the leg to prevent movement. It must be done precisely where there was injury; and move the leg each day to see if there is an abscess anywhere else; treat until he heals properly.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From bone fractures due to impact
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from fracture, but when bones are struck, there is always a chance of fracture and in the limbs, there can only be pain in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones rise over each other, place such bones on the ground like they want to go, and then put your foot under his at the point where the bones are raised, press it so much that they come back to their senses; then apply plaster and cover it up, and underneath the belly of the foot put a small board about two inches thick, then fix it against the foot arch, then wrap it with blankets around, and other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, you should release the bandage because you will find that the bones are even, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, restore them, as we have said about the ribs of the hand; then place on each broken rib a splint according to the length of that rib, and slightly larger than it, then set beneath the rib the table I mentioned, and apply the joint support over this. And if there are two or three or more broken ones, break them, placing on each one of these ribs a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen, and hold the table under the rib; and being placed at the head of the table facing the abdomen beneath it, ensure that it cuts well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I've said about other injuries, once we have discussed them; and assist each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of her nature break during childbirth, if she is allowed to sit in a larger position, then incline her towards the lower back section, and hold her at the rear. Next, fill the natural cavity with cotton from her condition, and also insert it quite generously; then stand up the woman, and lift her back slowly bit by bit, and then let out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of nature, and brings the bones back in line; and when she needs to urinate, if you remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put her back as usual, and repeat this process for seven or more days: then the break will heal. If you see fit, take a goat's bladder, tie it with a stick at one end, fill the bladder inside out according to nature; then blow into the stick until the bladder inflates internally: nature will correct the break; then fill it with cotton and leave her like that for some days, until she is restored.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand or arm is broken, or in the case of a woman if it's the bones of her arms and legs, then restore it as we have instructed with regard to the hipbone; and these nearby fractures should not be overlooked by someone who applies their effort and use, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And the breaking means in many positions the correct way of restoration: thus understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of the penis being broken, take an oyster shell and fill it with the penis; then wrap it in linen, and leave it for three days or as long as necessary, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	By fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it's large, like in the thigh or shoulder or similar places, that they be treated now, so that the treatments we have said can bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, use vitriol to bandage it up again, if you don't have anything else, then resume treating the fracture at the same hour or day. If no pus appears in the dressing, then proceed with restoring the fracture.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus appears in the dressing, let the restoration continue until the third day, as long as the pus is subsiding. Don't touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you might provoke a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you can see the broken bone above the opened part of the knee, it is necessary that you place them slightly together with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not visible for you to place them evenly with your hands, take this tool made of iron that measures seven or eight inches in length, and its width should match the size of the wound; it's necessary for the surgeon when needed three or four tools according to what they require for each treatment of broken limbs; make sure they are round and slightly larger, so they don't bend under pressure on your limb while working, and they should be sharp in front, and large at the center towards the front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche' because it requires that the curved heads be placed on the top of the visible bone; and push it once so that when it heals, it is equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the breakage is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it requires that you hold the top of the bone as long as the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place as we said before, if one has access to an appropriate instrument for this task, such as a file or saw, with your power; then remove what is remaining in the bone's roughness and small slices.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the flesh feels great pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you want to do so that it is in its place, then spread with meath oil a black, sticky liniment, and if it's for an external wound; and don't put any plaster or other thing with ointment on the wound when there's no pus, to prevent the development of gangrene and decay; then give this treatment after you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, applying a complete covering according to the size of the wound, and be very careful not to restrict the wound with pressure; many times people have done it this way, and they have caused either death or corrosion in the flesh. And make sure that the compresses are softer and more pliable than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that some injuries have occurred, as we said, and you find pain in the limb, it does not seem right to apply ointment; but cover inside, instead of applying ointment, wrap with hard cloths, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the pus has increased at the wound, remove what you have put in all the wine, and apply a healing ointment to the wounds, such as a tetracycline ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you dislocate the limb twice a day, at morning and at vespers, until it is joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be such that the limb be adjusted in this manner so that the bone moves down slightly without impediment.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this persists day after day and the bone cannot be joined back immediately, you must know that there are small fragments of bone causing this, so it is necessary for you to seek out the wound with a probe, and remove all these required fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a sinus tract comes to the limb, or any other manner of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he stated in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, such as the bones of the heel or shoulder, and others of the large limbs, you must not treat it because many die from it; but let it heal as long as it heals; perhaps it will drain out after twenty days or thirty, then you can treat the wound if possible; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The bruises that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The bruises often appear after the healing of the wound, especially near joints. A strange thing to see is the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot perform its natural tasks.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when this condition appears: if it is necessary to administer stomatic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, along with sarsaparilla, caraway, and other similar substances; do so by choosing any of these things or all together, and mix them with stomatic wine, or enough egg whites, or vinegar; then apply it on the nodule in poultices and press well, but don't remove from hands until days have passed; after that remove it, and start again with another application as long as the swellings are gone. Or you can apply it over a well-made piece of plaster; because the property of plaster is such that it removes all swellings on limbs; if the swelling has turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, cover it, show what is superfluous, or bring it to any surgeon until it is removed, and treat it until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which becomes weak after a siege (or prolonged period of stress or effort).
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after it stays, the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to various causes: one reason could be that it was bound too tightly and not released as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, thus preventing the proper movement in the limb; or perhaps from excessive bleeding; or due to overly large movements that didn't occur at their time; or because they lack blood within their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you eat the meat in him, and make the body tender, until the abscess multiplies within it; then give baths to him, and provide joy and ease; afterwards apply grease on the limb, so that the grease attracts to the large node, and washes it frequently with water, until the node matches up with the limb; and restore its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is bent after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly afterwards, it loses none of its natural function: do not believe those who say one must break the limb entirely anew. Many fools have done this in our land, and these procedures are criticized; they cause great harms and even death. Nonetheless, when the swelling and torture are fresh, you should use hot water to make them rise or cook mildifying herbs such as leaves of mallow, roots, and marigold, among similar treatments. Make one emplastre of a mildifying nature, like well-made aqua vitae, take mallow extract and mix it with grease from pork fat or oil of safflower, then make an emplastre. Alternatively, you can take fatty figs, grind them with buckwheat flour, and other medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is any bone moved by constant rubbing for long periods with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the member have some movement every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation has hardened and become tough like bone, requiring treatment with heat, if it's suitable to cover up until reaching the bone in surgery; and apply care and diligence in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none but suits for immediate repositioning without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, they swell the limbs, and by chance set them in bone; because it is not good to move the limb when it is swollen: many times pus and other pains are brought about. Nevertheless, when this happens, have a surgeon treat the patient, then leave him until all the pus has subsided; then immerse the member in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated backwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat bone-like at their roots, and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the bottom of the body, causing saliva from the mouth to escape, unable to contain it, and unable to close his mouth. Also, he envelops his tongue with his speech due to this condition.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it immediately without hesitation; and in such a manner that the servants cut off the head of the sick person, and insert needles into her pocket under the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts. And the other hand should be out from the hands to make them equal; and command the patient to soften her jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep pushing until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is painful, just the same, even when they are both mandibles together, if you heat with hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset it; do not overly force the repositioning, just as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought equally, and the mouth of the patient is well closed by being mollified, if you place moist cloths in a poultice made of rose oil and beeswax on them, then bind them lightly with moist threads; and let the patient lie on his back, and have his limbs between two cushions, so that he does not move or to the right nor to the left, nor tries to bend at all, but eats light food until the pains are eased, and the jaws are sewn; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not try to open his mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well stitched and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be properly aligned in an hour and are not turned back to their original positions, fever and settled discomfort result, often accompanied by bloating or vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then you know it's a loss; many times, death has befallen those who have experienced this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the forcefulness
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot alleviate from within the continuity of it and the bottom, and is dislocated every single time at the front, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the healing process is as follows: the patient lies on his back, and extends his arms. And in this manner, the shoulder blades of the spine are brought back when they have been removed from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On orders concerning the shoulder joint,
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: in one way it dislocates towards the side of the armpit downwards; and in another way it dislocates at the bottom part; and by chance dislocates upwards, which happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder or inside for nerves; and dislocates repeatedly down to the armpit, even with those who have little flesh because it goes quickly with them; with those who have enough flesh, it jumps over and comes back over.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some people a percussion or a breaking, and inflates the shoulder with an abscess, and believes that it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must prove it, as long as you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocations occur when one goes towards the armpit, and there's a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one; you will find various evident differences between them. You will discover a hollow in the top of the shoulder and from the armpit to the collarbone; just like if it were an eye. The patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor can they move at all. And similarly, if the shoulder is dislocated upwards, it doesn't disappear completely because you find it clearly at the collarbone. This type of dislocation can only be resolved, when new, or when a person's child is underaged; for this manner of dislocation cannot be otherwise removed.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministers lift their hand from under the malady at the top, then place their palms underneath it and lift the joint up to the shoulder with force; and they lift the hand, stretch it upwards, and put it back down under it; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come about as we have said after a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water. They should be treated with soothing and calming remedies: decoction of tea, fenugreek, and milk thistle in water should be used for bathing; they must then use this treatment method. After that, the patient's back should be wrapped with a warm cloth. Place a piece of soft but not too soft wool under the patient’s buttocks during this process, neither too soft nor too hard. Then place your fingers on the bottom of their foot against the wool, and gently raise their shoulder up, pulling down on their hand; others should cut the head of their shoulder softly to prevent it from moving downwards. This way, they get their shoulder back in place immediately. If you see that you have successfully reset it this way: and then make sure there's someone bigger than the patient present at home during this process. The patient should be straight towards their side, pushing their shoulder under the wool against the body, lifting the body upwards so that the patient hangs down; other helpers pull your hand down towards the belly of the patient.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if they are too light for the patient, there is nothing he can carry, and the dislocation simply returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it can also be done in another way: and you stick the long coal into the ground, so that the patient is held as if by a pistol, and not too thick or too soft; then place it under the body but let there be a shield underneath, and have the patient hold the position for the entire length of the stick; and extend your hand from the other side to form the joint again, and the dislocation will return to its place quickly; and if it doesn't return by all these methods that we've mentioned, then do this cure: take a firebrand of two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a handle that allows for movement through it near its base in front against the wall, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then cover the head with a cloth beneath, so that the head does not bruise the patient, then place it on the pillow under the patient; and stretch out your arms along the body of the patient, and place the shoulder in front, and lay the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one end of an inch of a board of about the width, and let the hands hang downwards on the other side: the joint is now restored.

Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation is in front, it's necessary to extend the painful leg quickly, and do as I've said; place the patient's pain on the inner side of their knee, then press with the other hand, and push down towards their ankle.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is behind, it does not suffice to lengthen the body downwards or lift him off the ground. Instead, he should be in such a position as when his hip was dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on both hips; and it should be under his buttocks, and the strap extended as we said earlier, and must press on the joint from the table; and will be ready when the body stretches its legs, and they will be even; then adjust the knees, put in the splint, and hold with one band, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three days or four, then release him, and place the splint on; and when you see that they are even, tighten again as before, and leave it for three days; then release him, let him walk properly, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Regarding shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees are dislocated in two ways: it means, internally and externally, and behind; and does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs indicate that you should instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee. If they cannot bend it towards their knee, know that their joint is dislocated; and in the restoration process, this means making the patient lie straight, extending their leg if possible, placing your back against their buttocks, and placing their foot on yours; then take hold of their knee with your hands, pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee towards each other. And another assistant should extend their foot until the knees return to their place, and the signs are that they bend well their leg slightly at their knee; and apply the bandage, make the leg rest against the knee, keep them together tightly for three or four days, then release them; and do not let the patient work with their limbs until their joints are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not intact, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	from the heel dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are neither fully set nor completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tries to move before it dislocates; the reduction should be quick, and one must gently extend its movement with their hands when it begins to settle.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is reduced as soon as possible, the patient should be made to lie straight, and hold their leg out by the foot, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then extend upwards, and firmly push the heel up; and repeat this twice, just like we said, while pushing and pulling on the heel. If it returns, that is well; if not, continue with the process as before, for it will return; and if it cannot return in such a manner, let the patient lie over their back on the ground, firmly place a stick between their thighs, and tie them tightly around to prevent bruising of the leg. Then shave the thigh, and another assistant extends the foot or another person with their hands or under the arm, which is tied onto the neck; then evenly extend each assistant's movement, and place the stick so it is tight between the thighs for the sake of keeping the heel when extended; then adjust the eyes equal to the dislocation on your hands, and another assistant shaves the healthy leg above the ankle, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it reaches the point, place the bandage and apply heat above, then hold firmly in shape, tie the leg to the foot and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, making sure not to tie too tightly; then leave for two or three days; if he loosens during this time, remove the tie. Then release on the third day or fourth, and advise walking the patient for four days; and if it goes beyond these limits, there's still no certainty that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are abscesses around, it is necessary to soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, while they are still swollen.
des dois	Of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two shoulders are reduced, if they fit well and extend in a proper manner, it is a simple task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in neither the neck nor the waist, then you must have the patient lie on their full length or on a table entirely straightened out, and place your foot where it opens from the joints, then press with your foot until it regains consciousness; and when it's even, and there isn't anything opening, then put under the heel of your foot a two-shoulder table, then hold in shape, and leave for three days, then release him; and have him rest until he is sound.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding injuries and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When disease comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you lack compassion and mercy, do not be rash; at the beginning use soothing things on abscesses, let the patient depend on God's hand, if you cannot see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, immediately reset the limb to its place in such a way that the abscesses are released as they come about; and once the limb is placed, administer soothing things on abscesses, treat the wound according to what should be done with desiccated ointments; and if there's breakage due to dislocation and small bones have been fractured, set them, and do what we've said in simple illnesses; and protect yourself from entering into fear's path, as I've said, because it will make you stumble according to your Creator, and for the wisdom it equips you with and the health of your body.
